</tr>
</table>
<p>A 2006 <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> forum presented costs for managing intermittency as a function of wind-energy's share of total capacity for several countries, as shown in the table on the right. Three reports on the wind variability in the UK issued in 2009, generally agree that variability of wind needs to be taken into account by adding 20% to the operating reserve, but it does not make the grid unmanageable. The additional costs, which are modest, can be quantified.<sup id="cite_ref-abbess_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abbess-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The combination of diversifying variable renewables by type and location, forecasting their variation, and integrating them with dispatchable renewables, flexible fueled generators, and demand response can create a power system that has the potential to meet power supply needs reliably. Integrating ever-higher levels of renewables is being successfully demonstrated in the real world:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>In 2009, eight American and three European authorities, writing in the leading electrical engineers' professional journal, didn't find "a credible and firm technical limit to the amount of wind energy that can be accommodated by electric power grids". In fact, not one of more than 200 international studies, nor official studies for the eastern and western U.S. regions, nor the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>, has found major costs or technical barriers to reliably integrating up to 30% variable renewable supplies into the grid, and in some studies much more.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <sup id="cite_ref-Lovins11_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lovins11-107">[106]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">Solar power</a> tends to be complementary to wind.<sup id="cite_ref-windsun_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-windsun-108">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smallWindSystems_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smallWindSystems-109">[108]</a></sup> On daily to weekly timescales, <a href="/wiki/High_pressure_area" class="mw-redirect" title="High pressure area">high pressure areas</a> tend to bring clear skies and low surface winds, whereas <a href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Low pressure area">low pressure areas</a> tend to be windier and cloudier. On seasonal timescales, solar energy peaks in summer, whereas in many areas wind energy is lower in summer and higher in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[nb 2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cleveland_water_crib_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland_water_crib-111">[109]</a></sup> Thus the seasonal variation of wind and solar power tend to cancel each other somewhat. In 2007 the Institute for Solar Energy Supply Technology of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kassel" title="University of Kassel">University of Kassel</a> pilot-tested a <a href="/wiki/Virtual_power_plant" title="Virtual power plant">combined power plant</a> linking solar, wind, <a href="/wiki/Biogas" title="Biogas">biogas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity" title="Pumped-storage hydroelectricity">hydrostorage</a> to provide load-following power around the clock and throughout the year, entirely from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-combined_power_plant_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combined_power_plant-112">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Predictability">Predictability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Predictability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_forecasting" title="Wind power forecasting">Wind power forecasting</a></div>
<p>Wind power forecasting methods are used, but predictability of any particular wind farm is low for short-term operation. For any particular generator there is an 80% chance that wind output will change less than 10% in an hour and a 40% chance that it will change 10% or more in 5&#160;hours.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, studies by Graham Sinden (2009) suggest that, in practice, the variations in thousands of wind turbines, spread out over several different sites and wind regimes, are smoothed. As the distance between sites increases, the correlation between wind speeds measured at those sites, decreases.<sup id="cite_ref-Diesendorf_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diesendorf-114">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thus, while the output from a single turbine can vary greatly and rapidly as local wind speeds vary, as more turbines are connected over larger and larger areas the average power output becomes less variable and more predictable.<sup id="cite_ref-huang_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huang-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Wind power hardly ever suffers major technical failures, since failures of individual wind turbines have hardly any effect on overall power, so that the distributed wind power is reliable and predictable,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (October 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> whereas conventional generators, while far less variable, can suffer major unpredictable outages.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_storage">Energy storage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Energy storage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">Grid energy storage</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_energy_storage_projects" title="List of energy storage projects">List of energy storage projects</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg/220px-Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg/330px-Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg/440px-Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="719" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adam_Beck_Complex.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Sir_Adam_Beck_Hydroelectric_Generating_Stations" title="Sir Adam Beck Hydroelectric Generating Stations">Sir Adam Beck Generating Complex</a> at <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_Ontario" title="Niagara Falls, Ontario">Niagara Falls, Canada</a>, includes a large <a href="/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity" title="Pumped-storage hydroelectricity">pumped-storage hydroelectricity reservoir</a>. During hours of low electrical demand excess <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical grid</a> power is used to pump water up into the reservoir, which then provides an extra 174 MW of electric power during periods of peak demand.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Typically, conventional <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> complements wind power very well. When the wind is blowing strongly, nearby hydroelectric stations can temporarily hold back their water. When the wind drops they can, provided they have the generation capacity, rapidly increase production to compensate. This gives a very even overall power supply and virtually no loss of energy and uses no more water.</p>
<p>Alternatively, where a suitable head of water is not available, <a href="/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity" title="Pumped-storage hydroelectricity">pumped-storage hydroelectricity</a> or other forms of <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid energy storage</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Compressed_air_energy_storage" title="Compressed air energy storage">compressed air energy storage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy_storage" title="Thermal energy storage">thermal energy storage</a> can store energy developed by high-wind periods and release it when needed. The type of storage needed depends on the wind penetration level&#160;– low penetration requires daily storage, and high penetration requires both short and long term storage&#160;– as long as a month or more. Stored energy increases the economic value of wind energy since it can be shifted to displace higher cost generation during peak demand periods. The potential revenue from this <a href="/wiki/Arbitrage" title="Arbitrage">arbitrage</a> can offset the cost and losses of storage. For example, in the UK, the 1.7 GW <a href="/wiki/Dinorwig_pumped_storage_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Dinorwig pumped storage plant">Dinorwig pumped-storage plant</a> evens out electrical demand peaks, and allows base-load suppliers to run their plants more efficiently. Although pumped-storage power systems are only about 75% efficient, and have high installation costs, their low running costs and ability to reduce the required electrical base-load can save both fuel and total electrical generation costs.<sup id="cite_ref-dinorwig_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dinorwig-117">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-futureStorage_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-futureStorage-118">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>In particular geographic regions, peak wind speeds may not coincide with peak demand for electrical power. In the U.S. states of <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_California" title="Wind power in California">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Texas" title="Wind power in Texas">Texas</a>, for example, hot days in summer may have low wind speed and high electrical demand due to the use of <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>. Some utilities subsidize the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_heat_pump" title="Geothermal heat pump">geothermal heat pumps</a> by their customers, to reduce electric power demand during the summer months by making air conditioning up to 70% more efficient;<sup id="cite_ref-geothermal_incentive_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geothermal_incentive-119">[117]</a></sup> widespread adoption of this technology would better match electric power demand to wind availability in areas with hot summers and low summer winds. A possible future option may be to interconnect widely dispersed geographic areas with an HVDC "<a href="/wiki/Super_grid" title="Super grid">super grid</a>". In the U.S. it is estimated that to upgrade the transmission system to take in planned or potential renewables would cost at least $60 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-slogin_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slogin-120">[118]</a></sup> while the society value of added windpower would be more than that cost.<sup id="cite_ref-usvis_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usvis-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Germany has an installed capacity of wind and solar that can exceed daily demand, and has been exporting peak power to neighboring countries, with exports which amounted to some 14.7 billion kilowatt hours in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_Welle-2012.11.11_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW_Welle-2012.11.11-121">[119]</a></sup> A more practical solution is the installation of thirty days storage capacity able to supply 80% of demand, which will become necessary when most of Europe's energy is obtained from wind power and solar power. Just as the EU requires member countries to maintain 90 days <a href="/wiki/Global_strategic_petroleum_reserves" title="Global strategic petroleum reserves">strategic reserves</a> of oil it can be expected that countries will provide electric power storage, instead of expecting to use their neighbors for net metering.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capacity_credit.2C_fuel_savings_and_energy_payback">Capacity credit, fuel savings and energy payback</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Capacity credit, fuel savings and energy payback">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The capacity credit of wind is estimated by determining the capacity of conventional plants displaced by wind power, whilst maintaining the same degree of system security.<sup id="cite_ref-The_facts_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_facts-123">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/American_Wind_Energy_Association" title="American Wind Energy Association">American Wind Energy Association</a>, production of wind power in the United States in 2015 avoided consumption of 73 billion gallons of water and reduced CO<sub>2</sub> emissions by 132 million metric tons, while providing $7.3 billion in public health savings.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The energy needed to build a wind farm divided into the total output over its life, <a href="/wiki/Energy_Return_on_Energy_Invested" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy Return on Energy Invested">Energy Return on Energy Invested</a>, of wind power varies but averages about 20–25.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> Thus, the energy payback time is typically around one year.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Wind turbines reached <a href="/wiki/Grid_parity" title="Grid parity">grid parity</a> (the point at which the cost of wind power matches traditional sources) in some areas of Europe in the mid-2000s, and in the US around the same time. Falling prices continue to drive the levelized cost down and it has been suggested that it has reached general grid parity in Europe in 2010, and will reach the same point in the US around 2016 due to an expected reduction in capital costs of about 12%.<sup id="cite_ref-businessgreen_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessgreen-129">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_power_cost_and_trends">Electric power cost and trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Electric power cost and trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png/220px-Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png/330px-Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png/440px-Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png 2x" data-file-width="844" data-file-height="506" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Danish_wind_power_LCOE_vs_wind_speed_in_2012.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Estimated cost per MWh for wind power in Denmark</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png/220px-US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png/330px-US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png/440px-US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png 2x" data-file-width="858" data-file-height="375" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_projected_cost_of_wind_power.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Laboratory" title="National Renewable Energy Laboratory">National Renewable Energy Laboratory</a> projects that the levelized cost of wind power in the U.S. will decline about 25% from 2012 to 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg/220px-Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg/330px-Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg/440px-Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A turbine blade convoy passing through <a href="/wiki/Edenfield" title="Edenfield">Edenfield</a> in the U.K. (2008). Even longer <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Blade_design" title="Wind turbine design">two-piece blades</a> are now manufactured, and then assembled on-site to reduce difficulties in transportation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Wind power is <a href="/wiki/Capital_intensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital intensive">capital intensive</a>, but has no fuel costs.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> The price of wind power is therefore much more stable than the volatile prices of fossil fuel sources.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Marginal_cost" title="Marginal cost">marginal cost</a> of wind energy once a station is constructed is usually less than 1-cent per kW·h.<sup id="cite_ref-Patel_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patel-133">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, the estimated <a href="/wiki/Average_cost" title="Average cost">average cost</a> per unit of electric power must incorporate the cost of construction of the turbine and transmission facilities, borrowed funds, return to investors (including cost of risk), estimated annual production, and other components, averaged over the projected useful life of the equipment, which may be in excess of twenty years. Energy cost estimates are highly dependent on these assumptions so published cost figures can differ substantially. In 2004, wind energy cost a fifth of what it did in the 1980s, and some expected that downward trend to continue as larger multi-megawatt <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">turbines</a> were mass-produced.<sup id="cite_ref-helming_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helming-134">[132]</a></sup> In 2012 capital costs for wind turbines were substantially lower than 2008–2010 but still above 2002 levels.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> A 2011 report from the American Wind Energy Association stated, "Wind's costs have dropped over the past two years, in the range of 5 to 6 cents per kilowatt-hour recently.... about 2 cents cheaper than coal-fired electric power, and more projects were financed through debt arrangements than tax equity structures last year.... winning more mainstream acceptance from Wall Street's banks.... Equipment makers can also deliver products in the same year that they are ordered instead of waiting up to three years as was the case in previous cycles.... 5,600 MW of new installed capacity is under construction in the United States, more than double the number at this point in 2010. Thirty-five percent of all new power generation built in the United States since 2005 has come from wind, more than new gas and coal plants combined, as power providers are increasingly enticed to wind as a convenient hedge against unpredictable commodity price moves."<sup id="cite_ref-salerno_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salerno-136">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>A British Wind Energy Association report gives an average generation cost of onshore wind power of around 3.2 pence (between US 5 and 6 cents) per kW·h (2005).<sup id="cite_ref-BWEA_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWEA-137">[135]</a></sup> Cost per unit of energy produced was estimated in 2006 to be 5 to 6 percent above the cost of new generating capacity in the US for coal and natural gas: wind cost was estimated at $55.80 per MW·h, coal at $53.10/MW·h and natural gas at $52.50.<sup id="cite_ref-eiadoe_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eiadoe-138">[136]</a></sup> Similar comparative results with natural gas were obtained in a governmental study in the UK in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-ccc_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-139">[137]</a></sup> In 2011 power from wind turbines could be already cheaper than fossil or nuclear plants; it is also expected that wind power will be the cheapest form of energy generation in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-nicola_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nicola-10">[10]</a></sup> The presence of wind energy, even when subsidised, can reduce costs for consumers (€5 billion/yr in Germany) by reducing the marginal price, by minimising the use of expensive <a href="/wiki/Peaking_power_plant" title="Peaking power plant">peaking power plants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-meritorder_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meritorder-140">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>An 2012 EU study shows <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_electricity_by_source" title="Cost of electricity by source">base cost</a> of onshore wind power similar to coal, when subsidies and <a href="/wiki/Externalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Externalities">externalities</a> are disregarded. Wind power has some of the lowest external costs.<sup id="cite_ref-eu2012_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eu2012-141">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2013 <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a> New Energy Finance (BNEF) reported that the cost of generating electric power from new wind farms is cheaper than new coal or new baseload gas plants. When including the current <a href="/wiki/Carbon_pricing_in_Australia" title="Carbon pricing in Australia">Australian federal government carbon pricing</a> scheme their modeling gives costs (in Australian dollars) of $80/MWh for new wind farms, $143/MWh for new coal plants and $116/MWh for new baseload gas plants. The modeling also shows that "even without a carbon price (the most efficient way to reduce economy-wide emissions) wind energy is 14% cheaper than new coal and 18% cheaper than new gas."<sup id="cite_ref-bnef.com.2F2013.2F02.2F07.2Frenewable-cheaper_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bnef.com.2F2013.2F02.2F07.2Frenewable-cheaper-142">[140]</a></sup> Part of the higher costs for new coal plants is due to high financial lending costs because of "the reputational damage of emissions-intensive investments". The expense of gas fired plants is partly due to "export market" effects on local prices. Costs of production from coal fired plants built in "the 1970s and 1980s" are cheaper than renewable energy sources because of depreciation.<sup id="cite_ref-bnef.com.2F2013.2F02.2F07.2Frenewable-cheaper_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bnef.com.2F2013.2F02.2F07.2Frenewable-cheaper-142">[140]</a></sup> In 2015 BNEF calculated LCOE prices per MWh energy in new powerplants (excluding carbon costs)&#160;: $85 for onshore wind ($175 for offshore), $66–75 for coal in the Americas ($82–105 in Europe), gas $80–100.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> A 2014 study showed unsubsidized <a href="/wiki/LCOE" class="mw-redirect" title="LCOE">LCOE</a> costs between $37–81, depending on region.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> A 2014 US DOE report showed that in some cases <a href="/wiki/Power_purchase_agreement" title="Power purchase agreement">power purchase agreement</a> prices for wind power had dropped to record lows of $23.5/MWh.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cost has reduced as wind turbine technology has improved. There are now longer and lighter wind turbine blades, improvements in turbine performance and increased power generation efficiency. Also, wind project capital and maintenance costs have continued to decline.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> For example, the wind industry in the USA in early 2014 were able to produce more power at lower cost by using taller wind turbines with longer blades, capturing the faster winds at higher elevations. This has opened up new opportunities and in Indiana, Michigan, and Ohio, the price of power from wind turbines built 300&#160;feet to 400&#160;feet above the ground can now compete with conventional fossil fuels like coal. Prices have fallen to about 4 cents per kilowatt-hour in some cases and utilities have been increasing the amount of wind energy in their portfolio, saying it is their cheapest option.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of initiatives are working to reduce costs of electric power from offshore wind. One example is the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_Trust" title="Carbon Trust">Carbon Trust</a> Offshore Wind Accelerator, a joint industry project, involving nine offshore wind developers, which aims to reduce the cost of offshore wind by 10% by 2015. It has been suggested that innovation at scale could deliver 25% cost reduction in offshore wind by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Stiesdal" title="Henrik Stiesdal">Henrik Stiesdal</a>, former Chief Technical Officer at Siemens Wind Power, has stated that by 2025 energy from offshore wind will be one of the cheapest, scalable solutions in the UK, compared to other renewables and fossil fuel energy sources, if the true cost to society is factored into the cost of energy equation.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> He calculates the cost at that time to be 43 EUR/MWh for onshore, and 72 EUR/MWh for offshore wind.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incentives_and_community_benefits">Incentives and community benefits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Incentives and community benefits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg/220px-GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg" width="220" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg/330px-GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg/440px-GreenMountainWindFarm_Fluvanna_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">U.S. landowners typically receive $3,000–$5,000 annual rental income per wind turbine, while farmers continue to grow crops or graze cattle up to the foot of the turbines.<sup id="cite_ref-nine_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nine-153">[151]</a></sup> Shown: the <a href="/wiki/Brazos_Wind_Farm" title="Brazos Wind Farm">Brazos Wind Farm</a>, Texas.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Wind_energy_converter5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Wind_energy_converter5.jpg/220px-Wind_energy_converter5.jpg" width="220" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Wind_energy_converter5.jpg/330px-Wind_energy_converter5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Wind_energy_converter5.jpg/440px-Wind_energy_converter5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Some of the 6,000 turbines in California's <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Pass_Wind_Farm" title="Altamont Pass Wind Farm">Altamont Pass Wind Farm</a> aided by tax incentives during the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-altamontPass_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-altamontPass-154">[152]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The U.S. wind industry generates tens of thousands of jobs and billions of dollars of economic activity.<sup id="cite_ref-usdept_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usdept-155">[153]</a></sup> Wind projects provide local taxes, or payments in lieu of taxes and strengthen the economy of rural communities by providing income to farmers with wind turbines on their land.<sup id="cite_ref-nine_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nine-153">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> Wind energy in many jurisdictions receives financial or other support to encourage its development. Wind energy benefits from <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">subsidies</a> in many jurisdictions, either to increase its attractiveness, or to compensate for subsidies received by other forms of production which have significant negative externalities.</p>
<p>In the US, wind power receives a production tax credit (PTC) of 1.5¢/kWh in 1993 dollars for each kW·h produced, for the first ten years; at 2.2 cents per kW·h in 2012, the credit was renewed on 2 January 2012, to include construction begun in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> A 30% tax credit can be applied instead of receiving the PTC.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> Another tax benefit is <a href="/wiki/Accelerated_depreciation" title="Accelerated depreciation">accelerated depreciation</a>. Many American states also provide incentives, such as exemption from property tax, mandated purchases, and additional markets for "<a href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_Certificates" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable Energy Certificates">green credits</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Energy_Improvement_and_Extension_Act_of_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy Improvement and Extension Act of 2008">Energy Improvement and Extension Act of 2008</a> contains extensions of credits for wind, including microturbines. Countries such as <a href="/wiki/Wind_Power_Production_Incentive" title="Wind Power Production Incentive">Canada</a> and Germany also provide incentives for wind turbine construction, such as tax credits or minimum purchase prices for wind generation, with assured grid access (sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Feed-in_tariff" title="Feed-in tariff">feed-in tariffs</a>). These feed-in tariffs are typically set well above average electric power prices.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> In December 2013 U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Alexander" title="Lamar Alexander">Lamar Alexander</a> and other Republican senators argued that the "wind energy production tax credit should be allowed to expire at the end of 2013"<sup id="cite_ref-Tax_Analysts_TNT-2013.12.17-243-20_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tax_Analysts_TNT-2013.12.17-243-20-163">[161]</a></sup> and it expired 1 January 2014 for new installations.</p>
<p>Secondary market forces also provide incentives for businesses to use wind-generated power, even if there is a <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_Certificates" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable Energy Certificates">premium price for the electricity</a>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">socially responsible manufacturers</a> pay utility companies a premium that goes to subsidize and build new wind power infrastructure. Companies use wind-generated power, and in return they can claim that they are undertaking strong "green" efforts. In the US the organization Green-e monitors business compliance with these renewable energy credits.<sup id="cite_ref-green-e_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-e-164">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Small-scale_wind_power">Small-scale wind power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Small-scale wind power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Microgeneration" title="Microgeneration">Microgeneration</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg/220px-Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg" width="220" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg/330px-Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg/440px-Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg 2x" data-file-width="451" data-file-height="581" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A small <a href="/wiki/Quietrevolution_wind_turbine" title="Quietrevolution wind turbine">Quietrevolution QR5</a> <a href="/wiki/Gorlov_helical_turbine" title="Gorlov helical turbine">Gorlov type</a> <a href="/wiki/Vertical_axis_wind_turbine" title="Vertical axis wind turbine">vertical axis wind turbine</a> on the roof of <a href="/wiki/Colston_Hall" title="Colston Hall">Colston Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol, England</a>. Measuring 3&#160;m in diameter and 5&#160;m high, it has a nameplate rating of 6.5&#160;kW.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Small-scale wind power is the name given to wind generation systems with the capacity to produce up to 50&#160;kW of electrical power.<sup id="cite_ref-smallScaleCarbonTrust_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smallScaleCarbonTrust-165">[163]</a></sup> Isolated communities, that may otherwise rely on <a href="/wiki/Diesel_generator" title="Diesel generator">diesel</a> generators, may use wind turbines as an alternative. Individuals may purchase these systems to reduce or eliminate their dependence on grid electric power for economic reasons, or to reduce their <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a>. Wind turbines have been used for household electric power generation in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">battery</a> storage over many decades in remote areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Dodge_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dodge-166">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recent examples of small-scale wind power projects in an urban setting can be found in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, where, since 2009, a number of building projects have capped their roofs with <a href="/wiki/Gorlov_helical_turbine" title="Gorlov helical turbine">Gorlov-type helical wind turbines</a>. Although the energy they generate is small compared to the buildings' overall consumption, they help to reinforce the building's 'green' credentials in ways that "showing people your high-tech boiler" can not, with some of the projects also receiving the direct support of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Energy_Research_and_Development_Authority" title="New York State Energy Research and Development Authority">New York State Energy Research and Development Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times-2014.05.27_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times-2014.05.27-167">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Grid-connected domestic wind turbines may use <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid energy storage</a>, thus replacing purchased electric power with locally produced power when available. The surplus power produced by domestic microgenerators can, in some jurisdictions, be fed into the network and sold to the utility company, producing a retail credit for the microgenerators' owners to offset their energy costs.<sup id="cite_ref-home-made_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-home-made-168">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>Off-grid system users can either adapt to intermittent power or use batteries, <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> or diesel systems to supplement the wind turbine. Equipment such as parking meters, traffic warning signs, street lighting, or wireless Internet gateways may be powered by a small wind turbine, possibly combined with a photovoltaic system, that charges a small battery replacing the need for a connection to the power grid.<sup id="cite_ref-Cleantechnica-2009.05.13_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cleantechnica-2009.05.13-169">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Carbon_Trust" title="Carbon Trust">Carbon Trust</a> study into the potential of small-scale wind energy in the UK, published in 2010, found that small wind turbines could provide up to 1.5 terawatt hours (TW·h) per year of electric power (0.4% of total UK electric power consumption), saving 0.6 million tonnes of carbon dioxide (Mt CO<sub>2</sub>) emission savings. This is based on the assumption that 10% of households would install turbines at costs competitive with grid electric power, around 12 pence (US 19 cents) a kW·h.<sup id="cite_ref-CarbonSmallTrust_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarbonSmallTrust-170">[168]</a></sup> A report prepared for the UK's government-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Energy_Saving_Trust" title="Energy Saving Trust">Energy Saving Trust</a> in 2006, found that home power generators of various kinds could provide 30 to 40% of the country's electric power needs by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Scientist-2006.01.21_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Scientist-2006.01.21-171">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Distributed_generation" title="Distributed generation">Distributed generation</a> from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_resource" title="Renewable resource">renewable resources</a> is increasing as a consequence of the increased awareness of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. The electronic interfaces required to connect renewable generation units with the <a href="/wiki/Utility" title="Utility">utility</a> system can include additional functions, such as the active filtering to enhance the power quality.<sup id="cite_ref-ActiveFiltering_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ActiveFiltering-172">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_effects">Environmental effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Environmental effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_wind_power" title="Environmental impact of wind power">Environmental impact of wind power</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg/220px-Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg/330px-Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg/440px-Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">Livestock</a> grazing near a wind turbine.<sup id="cite_ref-livestock_ignore_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-livestock_ignore-173">[171]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The environmental impact of wind power when compared to the environmental impacts of fossil fuels, is relatively minor. According to the <a href="/wiki/IPCC" class="mw-redirect" title="IPCC">IPCC</a>, in assessments of the <a href="/wiki/Life-cycle_greenhouse-gas_emissions_of_energy_sources" title="Life-cycle greenhouse-gas emissions of energy sources">life-cycle global warming potential of energy sources</a>, wind turbines have a <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> value of between 12 and 11 (<a href="/wiki/Gram" title="Gram">g</a>CO<sub>2</sub><a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_equivalent" title="Carbon dioxide equivalent">eq</a>/<a href="/wiki/KWh" class="mw-redirect" title="KWh">kWh</a>) depending on whether off- or onshore turbines are being assessed.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_2014_Annex_III_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_2014_Annex_III-174">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> Compared with other <a href="/wiki/Low_carbon_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Low carbon power">low carbon power</a> sources, wind turbines have some of the lowest <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">global warming potential</a> per unit of electrical energy generated.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>While a wind farm may cover a large area of land, many land uses such as agriculture are compatible with it, as only small areas of turbine foundations and infrastructure are made unavailable for use.<sup id="cite_ref-mar_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mar-177">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-British_Wind_Energy_Association_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-British_Wind_Energy_Association-178">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are reports of bird and bat mortality at wind turbines as there are around other artificial structures. The scale of the ecological impact may<sup id="cite_ref-Eilperin_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eilperin-179">[177]</a></sup> or may not<sup id="cite_ref-rspb_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rspb-180">[178]</a></sup> be significant, depending on specific circumstances. Prevention and mitigation of wildlife fatalities, and protection of <a href="/wiki/Peat_bogs" class="mw-redirect" title="Peat bogs">peat bogs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-blanketpeat_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blanketpeat-181">[179]</a></sup> affect the siting and operation of wind turbines.</p>
<p>Wind turbines generate some noise. At a residential distance of 300 metres (980&#160;ft) this may be around 45&#160;dB, which is slightly louder than a refrigerator. At 1.5&#160;km (1&#160;mi) distance they become inaudible.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> There are anecdotal reports of negative health effects from noise on people who live very close to wind turbines.<sup id="cite_ref-Gohlke_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gohlke-184">[182]</a></sup> Peer-reviewed research has generally not supported these claims.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toronto_Star-2009.12.15_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toronto_Star-2009.12.15-186">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CanWEA09_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CanWEA09-187">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United States Air Force and Navy have expressed concern that siting large wind turbines near bases "will negatively impact radar to the point that air traffic controllers will lose the location of aircraft."<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aesthetic aspects of wind turbines and resulting changes of the visual landscape are significant.<sup id="cite_ref-TK_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TK-189">[187]</a></sup> Conflicts arise especially in scenic and heritage protected landscapes.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_government">Central government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Central government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Setokazenooka-park01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Setokazenooka-park01.jpg/220px-Setokazenooka-park01.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Setokazenooka-park01.jpg/330px-Setokazenooka-park01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Setokazenooka-park01.jpg/440px-Setokazenooka-park01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="668" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Setokazenooka-park01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Part of the <a href="/wiki/Seto_Windhill" title="Seto Windhill">Seto Hill Windfarm</a> in Japan.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">Nuclear power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> are <a href="/wiki/Energy_subsidies" title="Energy subsidies">subsidized by many governments</a>, and wind power and other forms of renewable energy are also often subsidized. For example, a 2009 study by the Environmental Law Institute<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> assessed the size and structure of U.S. energy subsidies over the 2002–2008 period. The study estimated that subsidies to fossil-fuel based sources amounted to approximately $72 billion over this period and subsidies to renewable fuel sources totalled $29 billion. In the United States, the federal government has paid US$74&#160;billion for energy subsidies to support <a href="/wiki/R%26D" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;D">R&amp;D</a> for <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> ($50 billion) and <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a> ($24 billion) from 1973 to 2003. During this same time frame, <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> technologies and <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a> received a total of US$26&#160;billion. It has been suggested that a subsidy shift would help to level the playing field and support growing energy sectors, namely <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, wind power, and <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-per_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-per-191">[189]</a></sup> History shows that no energy sector was developed without subsidies.<sup id="cite_ref-per_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-per-191">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> (IEA) (2011), energy subsidies artificially lower the price of energy paid by consumers, raise the price received by producers or lower the cost of production. "Fossil fuels subsidies costs generally outweigh the benefits. Subsidies to renewables and low-carbon energy technologies can bring long-term economic and environmental benefits".<sup id="cite_ref-IEA-FS2011_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA-FS2011-192">[190]</a></sup> In November 2011, an IEA report entitled <i>Deploying Renewables 2011</i> said "subsidies in green energy technologies that were not yet competitive are justified in order to give an incentive to investing into technologies with clear environmental and energy security benefits". The IEA's report disagreed with claims that renewable energy technologies are only viable through costly subsidies and not able to produce energy reliably to meet demand.</p>
<p>In the U.S., the wind power industry has recently increased its lobbying efforts considerably, spending about $5 million in 2009 after years of relative obscurity in Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-LobbyingAfter_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LobbyingAfter-193">[191]</a></sup> By comparison, the U.S. nuclear industry alone spent over $650 million on its lobbying efforts and campaign contributions during a single ten-year period ending in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-spendingOnNuclear_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spendingOnNuclear-194">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Times-2010.03.05_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Times-2010.03.05-195">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McClatchy-2010.01.24_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClatchy-2010.01.24-196">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2011_Japanese_nuclear_accidents" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Japanese nuclear accidents">2011 Japanese nuclear accidents</a>, Germany's federal government is working on a new plan for increasing <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">renewable energy commercialization</a>, with a particular focus on offshore wind farms. Under the plan, large wind turbines will be erected far away from the coastlines, where the wind blows more consistently than it does on land, and where the enormous turbines won't bother the inhabitants. The plan aims to decrease Germany's dependence on energy derived from coal and nuclear power plants.<sup id="cite_ref-Der_Spiegel-2011.03.23_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Der_Spiegel-2011.03.23-197">[195]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg/220px-Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg/330px-Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg/440px-Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="307" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Public_Opinion_Wind_Farm_Redington_Mountain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Environmental group members are both more in favor of wind power (74%) as well as more opposed (24%). Few are undecided.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Surveys of public attitudes across <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and in many other countries show strong public support for wind power.<sup id="cite_ref-com_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-com-198">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vipublic_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vipublic-199">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eon_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eon-200">[198]</a></sup> About 80% of EU citizens support wind power.<sup id="cite_ref-thefacts_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thefacts-201">[199]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, where wind power has gained very high social acceptance, hundreds of thousands of people have invested in citizens' wind farms across the country and thousands of small and medium-sized enterprises are running successful businesses in a new sector that in 2008 employed 90,000 people and generated 8% of Germany's electric power.<sup id="cite_ref-emp_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emp-202">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soc_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soc-203">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although wind power is a popular form of energy generation, the construction of wind farms is not universally welcomed, often for <a href="/wiki/Aesthetics" title="Aesthetics">aesthetic</a> reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-mar_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mar-177">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-com_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-com-198">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vipublic_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vipublic-199">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eon_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eon-200">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thefacts_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thefacts-201">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UKPOS.26T_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKPOS.26T-204">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pollingreport_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollingreport-205">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, with some exceptions, there has been little opposition to the installation of inland wind parks. However, the projects to build offshore parks have been more controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup> In particular, the proposal of building the biggest offshore wind power production facility in the world in southwestern Spain in the coast of <a href="/wiki/Cadiz" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadiz">Cádiz</a>, on the spot of the 1805 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a><sup id="cite_ref-Engineer2003_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engineer2003-207">[205]</a></sup> has been met with strong opposition who fear for tourism and fisheries in the area,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup> and because the area is a war grave.<sup id="cite_ref-Engineer2003_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engineer2003-207">[205]</a></sup></p>
<table class="floatright" cellpadding="7" cellspacing="0" style="border:solid 1px #aaa;">
<caption><b>Which should be increased in Scotland?</b><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup></caption>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_1d77bcc8b9ca1d583340418c2bd9f7ab" id="timeline_1d77bcc8b9ca1d583340418c2bd9f7ab"></map><img usemap="#timeline_1d77bcc8b9ca1d583340418c2bd9f7ab" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/1d77bcc8b9ca1d583340418c2bd9f7ab.png" /></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In a survey conducted by <a href="/wiki/Angus_Reid_Public_Opinion" title="Angus Reid Public Opinion">Angus Reid Strategies</a> in October 2007, 89 per cent of respondents said that using renewable energy sources like wind or solar power was positive for <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, because these sources were better for the environment. Only 4 per cent considered using renewable sources as negative since they can be unreliable and expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> According to a Saint Consulting survey in April 2007, wind power was the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">alternative energy</a> source most likely to gain public support for future development in Canada, with only 16% opposed to this type of energy. By contrast, 3 out of 4 Canadians opposed nuclear power developments.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2003 survey of residents living around <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>'s 10 existing wind farms found high levels of community acceptance and strong support for wind power, with much support from those who lived closest to the wind farms. The results of this survey support those of an earlier Scottish Executive survey 'Public attitudes to the Environment in Scotland 2002', which found that the Scottish public would prefer the majority of their electric power to come from renewables, and which rated wind power as the cleanest source of renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup> A survey conducted in 2005 showed that 74% of people in Scotland agree that wind farms are necessary to meet current and future energy needs. When people were asked the same question in a Scottish renewables study conducted in 2010, 78% agreed. The increase is significant as there were twice as many wind farms in 2010 as there were in 2005. The 2010 survey also showed that 52% disagreed with the statement that wind farms are "ugly and a blot on the landscape". 59% agreed that wind farms were necessary and that how they looked was unimportant.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News-2010.10.19_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-2010.10.19-213">[211]</a></sup> Regarding <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, query responders consider <a href="/wiki/Power_pylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Power pylon">power pylons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cell_site" title="Cell site">cell phone towers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantations</a> more negatively than wind farms.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup> Scotland is planning to obtain 100% of electric power from renewable sources by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup></p>
<p>In other cases there is <a href="/wiki/Community_wind_energy" title="Community wind energy">direct community ownership of wind farm projects</a>. The hundreds of thousands of people who have become involved in Germany's small and medium-sized wind farms demonstrate such support there.<sup id="cite_ref-discovery_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discovery-216">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>This 2010 Harris Poll reflects the strong support for wind power in Germany, other European countries, and the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-com_198-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-com-198">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vipublic_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vipublic-199">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup></p>
<center>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Community">Community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Community_debate_about_wind_farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Community debate about wind farms">Community debate about wind farms</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG/450px-Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG" width="450" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG/675px-Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG/900px-Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1172" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wind turbines such as these, in <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>, England, have been opposed for a number of reasons, including aesthetics, by some sectors of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[218]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many wind power companies work with local communities to reduce environmental and other concerns associated with particular wind farms.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup> In other cases there is <a href="/wiki/Community_wind_energy" title="Community wind energy">direct community ownership of wind farm projects</a>. Appropriate government consultation, planning and approval procedures also help to minimize environmental risks.<sup id="cite_ref-com_198-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-com-198">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[223]</a></sup> Some may still object to wind farms<sup id="cite_ref-wind-watch.org_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wind-watch.org-226">[224]</a></sup> but, according to <a href="/wiki/The_Australia_Institute" title="The Australia Institute">The Australia Institute</a>, their concerns should be weighed against the need to address the threats posed by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and the opinions of the broader community.<sup id="cite_ref-Australia_Institue_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australia_Institue-227">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>In America, wind projects are reported to boost local tax bases, helping to pay for schools, roads and hospitals. Wind projects also revitalize the economy of rural communities by providing steady income to farmers and other landowners.<sup id="cite_ref-nine_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nine-153">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the UK, both the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="National Trust">National Trust</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_to_Protect_Rural_England" title="Campaign to Protect Rural England">Campaign to Protect Rural England</a> have expressed concerns about the effects on the rural landscape caused by inappropriately sited wind turbines and wind farms.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News-2012.03.14_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-2012.03.14-228">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EDP24-2012.04.30_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDP24-2012.04.30-229">[227]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitelee_panorama.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Whitelee_panorama.JPG/450px-Whitelee_panorama.JPG" width="450" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Whitelee_panorama.JPG/675px-Whitelee_panorama.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Whitelee_panorama.JPG/900px-Whitelee_panorama.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5429" data-file-height="1901" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitelee_panorama.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A panoramic view of the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Whitelee_Wind_Farm" title="Whitelee Wind Farm">Whitelee Wind Farm</a> with Lochgoin Reservoir in the foreground.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some wind farms have become tourist attractions. The <a href="/wiki/Whitelee_Wind_Farm" title="Whitelee Wind Farm">Whitelee Wind Farm</a> Visitor Centre has an exhibition room, a learning hub, a café with a viewing deck and also a shop. It is run by the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Science_Centre" title="Glasgow Science Centre">Glasgow Science Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WhiteleeWindfarm_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteleeWindfarm-230">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Denmark, a loss-of-value scheme gives people the right to claim compensation for loss of value of their property if it is caused by proximity to a wind turbine. The loss must be at least 1% of the property's value.<sup id="cite_ref-Danish-loss-of-value-scheme_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Danish-loss-of-value-scheme-231">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite this general support for the concept of wind power in the public at large, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_effects_of_wind_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental effects of wind power">local opposition</a> often exists and has delayed or aborted a number of projects.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> For example, there are concerns that some installations can negatively affect TV and radio reception and Doppler weather radar, as well as produce excessive sound and vibration levels leading to a decrease in property values.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> Potential broadcast-reception solutions include predictive interference modeling as a component of site selection.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[235]</a></sup> A study of 50,000 home sales near wind turbines found no statistical evidence that prices were affected.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[236]</a></sup></p>
<p>While aesthetic issues are subjective and some find wind farms pleasant and optimistic, or symbols of <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy independence</a> and local prosperity, protest groups are often formed to attempt to block new wind power sites for various reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-wind-watch.org_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wind-watch.org-226">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-239">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardianQA_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianQA-240">[238]</a></sup></p>
<p>This type of opposition is often described as <a href="/wiki/NIMBY" title="NIMBY">NIMBYism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup> but research carried out in 2009 found that there is little evidence to support the belief that residents only object to renewable power facilities such as wind turbines as a result of a "Not in my Back Yard" attitude.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Turbine_design">Turbine design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wind_power&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Turbine design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">Wind turbine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design" title="Wind turbine design">Wind turbine design</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_aerodynamics" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind turbine aerodynamics">Wind turbine aerodynamics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wind_turbine_int.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wind_turbine_int.svg/220px-Wind_turbine_int.svg.png" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wind_turbine_int.svg/330px-Wind_turbine_int.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wind_turbine_int.svg/440px-Wind_turbine_int.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
